  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_612067a5-fe1e-4ea8-91f7-1839d9495f1b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6746010809350971512">The Clave is pleased to announce the newest edition of the Nephilim’s oldest and most famous training manual: the Shadowhunter’s Codex. Since the thirteenth century, the Codex has been the young Shadowhunter’s best friend. When you’re being swarmed by demons it can be easy to forget the finer points of obscure demon languages or the fastest way to stop an attack of Raum de</span>
  <span id="freeText6746010809350971512" style="display:none">The Clave is pleased to announce the newest edition of the Nephilim’s oldest and most famous training manual: the Shadowhunter’s Codex. Since the thirteenth century, the Codex has been the young Shadowhunter’s best friend. When you’re being swarmed by demons it can be easy to forget the finer points of obscure demon languages or the fastest way to stop an attack of Raum demons. With the Codex by your side, you never have to worry. <br /><br /> Now in its twenty-seventh edition, the Codex covers it all: the history and the laws of our world; how to identify, interact with, and if necessary, kill that world’s many colorful denizens; which end of the stele is the end you write with. No more will your attempt to fight off rogue vampires and warlocks be slowed by the need to answer endless questions from your new recruits: What is a Pyxis? Why don’t we use guns? If I can’t see a warlock’s mark, is there a polite way to ask him where it is? Where do we get all our holy water? Geography, History, Magic, and Zoology textbook all rolled into one, the Codex is here to help new Shadowhunters navigate the beautiful, often brutal world that we inhabit. <br /><br /> Do not let it be said that the Clave is outdated or, as the younger Shadowhunters say, “uncool”: this new edition of the Codex will be available not only in the usual magically-sealed demonskin binding, but also in a smart, modern edition using all of today’s most exciting printing techniques, including such new features as a sturdy clothbound cover, a protective dust jacket, and information about title, author, publisher, and so on conveniently available right on the cover. You’ll be pleased to know that it fits neatly into most satchels, and unlike previous editions, it rarely sets off alarm wards. <br /><br /> The old woodcuts and engravings have been replaced as well: instead, you’ll find lavish modern illustrations by some of the brightest luminaries of the fantastic. Creatures, weapons, people, and places have been carefully and accurately rendered by the likes of Rebecca Guay, Charles Vess, Jim Nelson, Theo Black, Elisabeth Alba, and Cassandra Jean. Chapters are beautifully introduced by the drawings of Michael Kaluta, and along with our condensation of the classic 2,450-page tome, A History of the Nephilim, you will find a selection of the best of the lovely illustrations of that volume by John Dollar. <br /><br /> This edition of the Codex will be available in Institute libraries and what mundanes sometimes call “book stores” in October 2013.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6746010809350971512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div id=buyButtonContainer class="uitext buttons buyableFeature u-marginTopXSmall u-paddingBottomXSmall u-bottomGrayBorder" data-book-id=13568619 >

    <div class="u-positionRelative">

  <span id="freeText10004719876163323715" style="display:none">1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2008644944" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Bones</a> ★★★<br />2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2373838717" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Ashes</a> ★★<br />3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2463489480" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Glass</a> ★★★<br />1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2465856942" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockwork Angel</a> ★★★<br />4.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2489169365" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Fallen Angels</a> ★<br />2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2518308849" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockwork Prince</a> ★★★★<br />5.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2526157370" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Lost Souls</a> ★★★★<br />3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2531117647" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockwork Princess</a> ★★★★★<br />6.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2544728646" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Heavenly Fire</a> ★★★★★<br />*.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2552335362" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bane Chronicles</a> ★★★<br />*.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564114842" rel="nofollow noopener">Tales from the Shadowhunter Academy</a> ★★★<br />1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2570227019" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Midnight</a> ★★★★★<br />2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2589314651" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of Shadows</a> ★★★★<br />3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425149252" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen of Air and Darkness</a> ★★★★<br /><br />Okay, I’m not going to write up a big review for this because honestly? I was a little bored while reading this and I kept forcing myself to pick it up! I did think the illustrations were absolutely beautiful! And I loved the addition of the scribbles and doodles in the margins, so we can see what some of our beloved characters thought while reading this book that is supposed to be an actual book in the Shadowhunter world. But, sadly, it reads like a textbook. But I am happy I read it, because I do think it not only expanded my knowledge of the world, but a few parts were actually interesting. But I for sure think you do not *need* to read this by any means whatsoever. <br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>

Her work is not extensive or deep or sophisticated or complicated enough to warrant both a book of critical essays and a comprehensive supplementary guide devoted to them. <div id="review_754729120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754729120" />
    <a title="Andre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6431131-andre"><img alt="Andre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378118123p2/6431131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754729120?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre" href="/user/show/6431131-andre">Andre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=don-t-read-it">don-t-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=beastmen">beastmen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754729120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17350175476745000740">This book was too stupid for too many reasons (listing them alone would hit the character limit so I will only mention a selected few examples in the spoiler sections, you can find a longer list here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://fav.me/d6w6853'>http://fav.me/d6w6853</a>). I hope I will never again read such a bad book.<br/>The start reads like the beginning of a Pokemon game, which is good for those games but not for a book like this<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ that claims to be a book every Hunter knows but clearly addresses only those that either have not ye</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17350175476745000740" style="display:none">This book was too stupid for too many reasons (listing them alone would hit the character limit so I will only mention a selected few examples in the spoiler sections, you can find a longer list here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fav.me/d6w6853">http://fav.me/d6w6853</a>). I hope I will never again read such a bad book.<br />The start reads like the beginning of a Pokemon game, which is good for those games but not for a book like this<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that claims to be a book every Hunter knows but clearly addresses only those that either have not yet or will later drink from the Mortal Cup (which was missing at the time this book was written; the later statement of it being officially labeled "misplaced" was one of a huge array of examples of Hunter idiocy) and become Shadowhunters. Furthermore this book addresses people from around the world, but all the name suggestions are in English. We also never get told why there are names like "Lightwood" if their names are supposed to be inconspicuous. And what about all the Britain references like comparing the Accords with the Bill of Rights if this is supposed to be an international book? Do they expect the readers to just know what that is? If yes it's even odder that they have to explain what a sword is, because I am pretty sure that more people will know the meaning of "sword" than "Bill of Rights". And let's say there are versions in other languages, why was that never addressed in this book? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It definitely isn't "the young Shadowhunter's best friend" as the advertisement claims.<br /><br />I guess the book is supposed to be some sort of field manual for warriors but apart from having the labels "milking the cash cow" and "self-insertion fantasy" written all over it I cannot say anything for sure. The space isn't even used well. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The artwork and "Q&amp;A" sections are mostly useless and they have stuff like names and runes listed in a very space consuming fashion (names are all written one below the other). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And based on the book itself this is a "corrected" version by Clary, which only highlights her stupidity/egoism because her "corrections" are either non-present<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (no extra info about the angel Raziel and she only gloated with her ability to make new runes) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> or what she wrote clashed with what was written in the other books<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (If gay marriage is legal in Idris, why is their society so allegedly homophobic as Isabelle claimed in City of Bones?) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, respectively it was stuff only fans would care about<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, like when she states that she had an icepack on her hips from training with Jace <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I guess some stuff is supposed to be comic relief, but it is so idiotic that they let the Hunters appear like lunatics <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, like Magnus's 17 reasons why people become Shadowhunters or the fact that the two examples for <i>more colorful means</i> of appointing their representatives in the Council include a dance competition and a giant chess tournament where the biggest looser is the representative <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Or it's completely useless, like the banter of Clary &amp; Co. <br />Some flaws and quirks in a made up world <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like the Clave's refusal to combine runes with warlock magic <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> could actually flesh out a world, make it look more real, but if there was such an attempt here, it was rendered meaningless by the sheer amount of flaws this world-building has. And apart from its flaws, the whole book often screamed laziness. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For instance:<br />There are no original fighting/combat styles, it's all taken from the mundanes.<br />The demon chapter did not read like a guide for future warriors, e.g. it doesn't contain common defenses against the different demons and the descriptions do not fit the danger level of the demons (the more dangerous, the more info you need). And the names are not only crap but a global order of demon-Hunters should have a much wider variety of demon names and they should match their real world counterparts. <br />The "origin" of the werewolves was basically "demon came -&gt; creates -&gt; leaves," that's it. There aren't even oral tales of what happened or anything, it doesn't concern anybody, despite the whole thing reeking of a hidden plan, just like the origin story of the vampires. Here the first vampire is Vlad Tepez III (aka Dracula aka biggest cliché in the genre) and they were created by the demon Hecate, which makes no sense at all. To make it as short as possible: She was variously associated with crossroads, entrance-ways, fire, light, the Moon, magic, witchcraft, knowledge of herbs and poisonous plants, necromancy, and sorcery, a protective goddess and one who bestowed prosperity and daily blessings on the family. And while the book gets the connection to witchcraft right the fact remains that she is a very bad choice as creator of the vampires. Not only are there the associations I stated (which often run completely counter to the image of the vampire) but also because of the animal most associated with her: the dog! Hecate would have made way more sense as creator of the werewolves.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There is also this constant theme that the Hunters are better than the "mundanes"<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ like having no such <i> uncivilized mundane notions</i> as political parties and being trained to be faster and stronger than mundanes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And naturally the book states them to be connected to all world religions, despite it being obvious that this franchise does not acknowledge the legitimacy of those belief systems<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, since that is basically what you do when you call upon the names of angels to power your blades, speak mostly of demons from Judeo-Christian folklore, turn Hecate into a demon and state "Kali" as a name of Lilith from Jewish folklore, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Every halfway decent idea<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, like color coding your special arrows, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is ruined by the Hunters' incredible incompetence that makes them look even more idiotic than previous books already did (no global order of warriors would ever act this way).<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They don't even use firearms (the reason is still "mark + gunpowder = no ignition") despite gold being poisonous to demons so even gold-coated bullets/weapons should have some effect, the same for the other metals for the Downworlders. They also usually fight in short, improvised confrontations, close quarter, rather than in planned battles; against enemies that can spit acid, breathe fire, fire projectiles, do spells, are super strong and fast and they literally say that demons are of infinite variety. They rarely use bows from a save range but rather in the midst of chaotic battle, which is practically suicide. The useless art of throwing daggers is widely practiced just for showing off, but all we get to the question why they don't just use water cannons against demons (water disrupts their magic,) is "it doesn't work like that," despite the fact that it is stated that holy water is severely toxic to demons. And despite all this stupidity the book claims that they prioritize detailed assessment of the environment and learn to avoid harm by wits and reflexes. This lack of planning and inventiveness only makes them look like incompetent morons.<br />And despite being an order with members from all over the place, they don't have a common language apart from the "language of Raziel and the Gray Book" aka the runes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Basically according to this book there are several things that could aid them against the demons. But do these morons use that to their full advantage? Not according to this book.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />And if Downworlders and Hunters are sworn to secrecy and can even claim specific rights and reparations because of the Accords than the entire franchise is a testament to the impotence of these Accords, since no side acts accordingly!<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The artwork is of decent quality but for the most part totally misplaced and often nothing but fan-service since it adds nothing to the book<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, or can anybody here tell me a good reason why all those pictures of Clary, Jace &amp; Co. are there? Several pictures clash with the books: e.g Magnus has a different built, mostly light hair, moderate clothes and the wrong eyeshape and Luke's wolf form isn't even black (no werewolf picture fits). The art on the "mundanes" was downright insulting and said "the world = USA" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. At least the grammar was ok, even if the wording was often weird. <br /><br />Actually I don't know when this book is supposed to have been read by Clary in-universe, I guess between City of Glass and City of Fallen Angels<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, since Clary plans to ask her mother regarding the protection ritual on new born Hunters <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but I have my doubts due to the convoluted material.<br />And convoluted fits this book to the last letter. A book like this is there to answer questions that were raised while reading the novels. But this book doesn't do that, at all. It flat out contradicts several elements of the other books of the franchise. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For instance:<br />The parabatai connection is allegedly very special and serious (but still the vow is made when the involved are kids) but the books never showed that and now it is stated that romantic bonds between parabatai is forbidden since it evokes magical harm. If that is the case then why is Alec still ok?<br />In City of Ashes Luke could kill a demon by hitting it with a truck, but here mundane weapons allegedly cannot harm them permanently (later they say enough blunt force can kill everything).<br />The book says werewolves look no different in human form, but City of Lost Souls states that their eyes have the <i>gold-ringed pupils of lycanthropy.</i><br />Now their transformation is described as painful and graphic (falling out teeth and all), but we got that only in City of Ashes, nowhere else, not even when werewolves were seen transforming by others.<br />Here vampires generally look <i>pale, sallow and thin, as though weakened by malnourishment or some wasting disease</i> but in other books their beauty was often noted and none was ever said to look malnourished or something. And just like pretty much every book since City of Bones, this one here totally ignores that the vampires in City of Bones were said to have <i>hands that curled into claws at the tips</i> and being able to transform into bats, mist and rat form. And not only where they shown to be transformed into bats by stating <i>above flew the vampires, hissing and screeching, filling the night with predatory cries</i>, that they can transform into rats was a plot point, it was the reason they thought transformed Simon was one of their own.<br />And if the unhallowed cannot enter an Institute, how could Luke in TMI? According to this book physically he is a run-of-the-mill werewolf.<br />Allegedly "many original members" and many of "the closest of Morgenstern's original followers" had fled from him before the Accords, but who? The other books only talked about Jocelyne and still no one warned the Clave? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />It is remarkable how little these Hunters know based on this book. How is it possible to fight demons and Downworlder for about a millennium and still know so little? On the other hand if they have no actual record of any summoning and even claim to know least about angels than any other supernatural creature, then how do they know all these does and don'ts and other stuff regarding angels? <br /><br />The book contradicts itself several times so often I lost count in fact. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br />During the first years of the vampires <i>chaos arose, as neither Nephilim nor vampires yet understood how new vampires were made</i>. And this after saying that Vlad &amp; Co had already created new vampires and that new ones popped up as quickly as old ones disappeared.<br />The offspring of a human and a fey is human (often with some "fey characteristics") not fey but the book states a few pages later that they abduct humans to be <i>used to produce new faerie children</i>. Would such offspring be stated to be half-fey I would say "ok, that makes sense" but that is not what the book states, the book states at first that the offspring of such a mix is human and later that its used to produce new faeries.<br />In the werewolf chapter they state that werewolves do not pass on their condition to their children (previous books suggested otherwise) and later on there is constant talk about inherited werewolf traits. So is the condition inheritable to not? Or is the offspring of even two werewolves some human werewolf mix?<br />This makes even less sense considered that the Mortal Cup can be used to kill Downworlders because ingesting the fluid makes the "demonic and angelic war fruitlessly" within them. The same mechanics causes stillbirths for Nephilim-demon mixes according to the book, so why can Hunters mix with fey and werewolves?<br />How can a Hunter become a Forsaken by stripping its Marks? The book says that allegedly they are made mundane by stripping them from their Marks and later that a child of Hunter who is "stripped" is still a Hunter by blood, so how could they say only pages before that they make some into mundanes as a punishment by taking away their marks?<br />If Lilith is the mother of demons and she was Adams first wife then how on earth can demons be older than humans? They say themselves that the oldest Nephilim texts say that Lilith was Adam's first wife. Are we to assume that Lilith was a demon from the beginning, became Adam's wife and "rejected the ways of mortals?" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />There is no sense over the course of several chapters and basically way more questions are raised than answered. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like:<br />Why are there only seraph blades and not other weapon types?<br />If Rowan, Ash and Oak are so often used by Hunters, why don't they have big forests planted?<br />Why is a chart showing the different demon frequencies a waste of time? If useless in the field, just learn the chart by heart and you won't have to go through the dangerous experience of recognizing demons by sight. Modern sensors have mapping systems, proximity alarms and other colorful features but no screen to show the demons they detect?<br />Why did it take until the 1960s for rune miniaturization magic to appear and make the sensors smaller? Where did that "magic" (the stuff they allegedly don't use, btw. they literally state here that their marks are magic) come from?<br />Why can the sensor detect demons but not Downworlders when they have demon magic installed in their souls?<br />If demons can be repelled by holy symbols why don't Hunters wear those all the time?<br />If no Forsaken has ever been turned into a Hunter by drinking from the Cup why do they even state this is an alternative to killing them?<br />How is it possible to place newborn Hunters under protection spells to strengthen them for receiving Marks if the only magic they have are the marks and the Mortal Instruments?<br />If Hunters are so few and die so young, why is there a law against marrying mundanes, and why no polygamy or more recruitment? Seriously they once recruited whole families and in the Middle Ages they had a lower infant mortality rate due to their rituals. People would have signed up in droves just for that.<br />And how does Idris even function? Who grows food, who builds houses? Who repairs stuff? Etc.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />What you see of world building here is basically what you already know from the other books and the new stuff mostly either contradicts these books, doesn't add anything or clearly wasn't reflected in the books. As a matter of fact it is incredible how little they know about so many topics. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They don't even know the original name or origin of their founder, just calling him Jonathan Shadowhunter, and the story how they came to be contradicts facts from the book (e.g. being able to fight successfully against demons with mundane weapons). The origin story contradicts City of Bones (there Raziel was summoned by a warlock). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Real world history and psychology is basically ransacked<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, allegedly magic and superstition has no influence today anymore, despite both being widespread over all continents, the first demon invasion allegedly caused the crusades because people thought all those corporal demons are there because the Holy Land is not in Christian hands. That example of a fake angel was utterly ridiculous for too many reasons to list here. And the whole chapter on mundanes was basically:<br />a) mundanes are idiots and of no use<br />b) pity mundanes for it, we have to protect them<br />The book even speaks as if the Mayan Empire still exists, could not find a better female role model than Boadicea (btw. if one of the first 3 Shadowhunters was already a female warrior why did the women need centuries to achieve equality?), claims Idris has totally unspoiled nature, that other major religious traditions have stories that may be talking about Lilith and Sammael and the story of the first Hunters in the Americas is a bad copy of the Mayflower stuff (down to the harsh winters and the helpful "first people") just like the story of the "lost Ethiopian Nephilim" who still kept the way is a rip-off of the story of the Beta Israel. They even have "Scorpion-Riders" in mid-1600s Australia. And I am not commenting about the story in 1199 Ireland; that breaks too many laws.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the Hunters come along as incompetent idiots that should have been wiped out a long time ago, or better they would be if the demons weren't even bigger idiots. <br /><br />The main heroes of the franchise come along either as idiots as well or simply assholes who care about nothing but themselves (based on what is presented here all of them should react quite differently <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, e.g. in City of Bones some holy water for Simon to drink would have been enough to negate the effects of the vampire blood that he had consumed and it wasn't as if that was something Jace shouldn't have known, this book is a revised edition of 2002 and City of Bones played in 2007 and it was clear that Simon had bitten vampires at least 6 times. Jace didn't even report this to anyone which according to this book he would have been obliged to do and he would have also been forbidden to ruin those vampire motorbikes, actually the vampires could have demanded reparations for that under the law. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br />And thank gosh I am not one of Raziel's chosen. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He didn't even give the Hunters the seraph blades, the only weapons that according to this book can permanently injure a demon (marked weapons only make them retreat to lick their wounds) right away, instead they had to "discover" them later by, well chance is the best word. And not only do they cause mundanes to burn to death, they even burn Hunters unless appropriately marked as well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That angel seems to be the biggest idiot and/or asshole in the entire universe.<br />I guess often the book tried to be "different"<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, like when demonic cults are stated as mostly harmless and only raising weaker demons, respectively ending in the participants being killed by the summoned demons, (why demons don't use cults to strengthen their foothold in the human world is anyone's guess) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but the result is that huge sections of the book screamed of bad-copying, unoriginal ideas, rip-offs, lip service to diversity and equality<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ which downright fail since not only are Hunters clearly claimed to be better than mundanes time and again, Clary &amp; Co do not object to the actually racist crap in the book and even Jonathan Shadowhunter was born special (allegedly the 7th son of a 7th son and of noble birth). And don't get me started on the "feminism" in this book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, pure laziness and lack of a competent editor and constructive criticism.<br />Would I be a fan of these characters, I would hate this book.<br /><br />PS: This is not a rip-off of "Fantastic Beasts and Where to find them". That book was a nice short mix of information and comic relief. This here was a worse example of world-building than Stephenie Meyer's Twilight Guide.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17350175476745000740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1086531184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086531184" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19673751-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540301866p2/19673751.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText3482058181366965188" style="display:none"><b>4.3/5</b><br /><br />Short story: I finally finished this book. Here is why it took me this long lol<br />So I was reading this book on my train trip when I went to the Shadowhunters convention this July. Then the post convention depression got me and this book reminded me too much of that period. So I put it on hold even because I was missing the last two chapters full of history dates and infos and the Law chapter which was as everything interesting but "heavier" as a subject.<br />Now I found motivation to finish it, so here it is, I did it 😂😂<br />____<br /><br />This book is SO informative, it's full of details, history and "curiosities", plus Jace, Clary and Simon comments that me laugh so hard more than once. I can totally see this as a text book, because that's the feeling I had while reading it. For personal taste I of course found some chapters more interesting than others, but I can't deny that this is very interesting and it's definitely a very good exapansion to this amazing universe!</span>

<div id="review_534463157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/534463157" />
    <a title="Carolina Carriço" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14877543-carolina-carri-o"><img alt="Carolina Carriço" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537987831p2/14877543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/534463157?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolina Carriço" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolina Carriço" href="/user/show/14877543-carolina-carri-o">Carolina Carriço</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer534463157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3481768282745859391"><b>The Shadowhunter's Codex was so, so good!</b><br/><br/>I started the book thinking that it was for Shadowhunter's like some kind of Bible, and then I understood that the point of creating a Codex was for new Shadowhunter's, mundanes who became Shadowhunters, or for kids adopted by Shadowhunters, and I was kinda disappointed. But when I got truly sucked up into it, <b>I was in love!</b><br/><br/>The way the Codex shows us the Shadow World is truly magical, and if I wanted to Shadowhunter's to be real first, and became one of t</span>
  <span id="freeText3481768282745859391" style="display:none"><b>The Shadowhunter's Codex was so, so good!</b><br /><br />I started the book thinking that it was for Shadowhunter's like some kind of Bible, and then I understood that the point of creating a Codex was for new Shadowhunter's, mundanes who became Shadowhunters, or for kids adopted by Shadowhunters, and I was kinda disappointed. But when I got truly sucked up into it, <b>I was in love!</b><br /><br />The way the Codex shows us the Shadow World is truly magical, and if I wanted to Shadowhunter's to be real first, and became one of them, now I wanted even more! I understand their ways and thoughts, their history as well, and it's beautiful! <br /><br />I, of course, knew about Jonathan Shadowhunter story and the rising of Raziel and the Mortal Instruments, but learning the story of the first two parabatai, and Silent Brother and Iron Sister made the original story even better! That was one of my favourite things about the Codex.<br /><br />Another think I loved was that it <b>made me laugh</b> every five pages or so. Not just the notes written by Clary, Simon and Jace are super funny, the Codex itself has it's own comments and irony through out the whole book.<br /><br />Finally, the images are freaking beautiful. Both the ones made by Clary and the ones the original Codex had!<br /><br />What I didn't like was that Codex instead of naming parabatai rune, <b>Parabatai</b> it named it friendship rune! Like it was that vulgar! <b>IT IS NOT</b><br /><br />One think I thought that the Codex should have is the meaning of the runes. It has images and their names, but most of them I have no idea what kind of use it can have. For example, what is the use for a Agony rune? Or a Bridge Rune?<br /><br /><i>Anyway, I loved the Codex! And I wish Cassandra Clare would write more books about Shadowhunter's culture and history. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3481768282745859391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3371586350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9215565484450533141">I gave this a high rating even though I really didn’t need to. <br/>I wasn’t really impressed per say because I knew everything in this book having read all the Shadowhunter books. That being said, it has some good info with some excerpts from our TMI characters in it. Those parts were funny and on character. But the book got really boring really fast, and unless you want something to help you understand the world better, this is a good tool with beautiful artwork in it. If you don’t choose to read i</span>
  <span id="freeText9215565484450533141" style="display:none">I gave this a high rating even though I really didn’t need to. <br />I wasn’t really impressed per say because I knew everything in this book having read all the Shadowhunter books. That being said, it has some good info with some excerpts from our TMI characters in it. Those parts were funny and on character. But the book got really boring really fast, and unless you want something to help you understand the world better, this is a good tool with beautiful artwork in it. If you don’t choose to read it though, that’s okay since whatever you learn in this book also comes up in the books books on their own, so you don’t have to worry if you are or are not getting extra info, because you aren’t really getting much. <br /><br />I gave this way too high of a rating but I’ll stick with it: 4 stars </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DpxAZwGX7edoOSJxFRU/EQzjftJlPZzlw5PlRfnimtDtfrUSu9+2yk654DF3EUX+VuqjUOXF1bnODiZXTZCdPQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VLC+KvoW2QuAcF5eZ2Lpxwx0v0nX3YOiLTfAvC39VnC3UktfQF6CJqbwnB4FZpMoVn1iy1clyv4gqgOumY9RnQ==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText5125038100945808520" style="display:none">Hello Goodreadsers. Here's my official bio:<br /><br />"Cassandra Clare was born overseas and spent her early years traveling around the world with her family and several trunks of fantasy books. Cassandra worked for several years as an entertainment journalist for the Hollywood Reporter before turning her attention to fiction. She is the author of City of Bones, the first book in the Mortal Instruments trilogy and a New York Times bestseller. Cassandra lives with her fiance and their two cats in Massachusetts."<br /><br />You can find me online at <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.cassandraclare.com">www.cassandraclare.com</a><br /><br />I have a blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/">http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/</a><br /><br />and a Facebook:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare">http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare</a><br /><br />and a Twitter:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/cassieclare">www.twitter.com/cassieclare</a><br /><br />I'll be available here on Goodreads to answer questions for a Goodreads Author Discussion starting September 18 — <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/37113.Q_A_with_Cassandra_Clare">http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/3...</a><br /><br />Go sign up so you don't miss the conversation when it starts!</span>
